Original Deviation Description (verbatim from spec-fidelity.md)\n    14→\n    15→> **ID**: DEV-001\n    16→> **Severity**: HIGH\n    17→> **Deviation**: Roadmap restructures the file layout with a `steps/` subdirectory and renames `commands.py` to `cli.py`, adding new modules (`contract.py`, `resume.py`, `convergence.py`) not in the spec, while omitting spec-defined files (`commands.py`, `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, `diagnostics.py`)\n    18→> **Spec Quote**: Section 4.1 New Files table lists 13 files including: `cli_portify/commands.py` (\"Click CLI group and `run` subcommand\"), `cli_portify/tui.py` (\"Rich live dashboard with gate state machine\"), `cli_portify/logging_.py` (\"Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging\"), `cli_portify/diagnostics.py` (\"DiagnosticCollector, FailureClassifier, ReportGenerator\")\n    19→> **Roadmap Quote**: \"New Modules (14 total)\" lists: `cli.py`, `contract.py`, `resume.py`, `convergence.py`, and `steps/validate_config.py` through `steps/panel_review.py` — no `commands.py`, `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, or `diagnostics.py`\n    20→> **Impact**: Four spec-defined modules are missing from the roadmap. The roadmap introduces three modules (`contract.py`, `resume.py`, `convergence.py`) that are not in the spec's architecture. The `steps/` subdirectory layout contradicts the spec's flat module structure. Implementers following the roadmap will produce a different file tree than the spec defines.\n    21→> **Recommended Correction**: Align the roadmap's file list to the spec's Section 4.1 table. Either (a) restore `commands.py`, `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, `diagnostics.py` and remove `contract.py`, `resume.py`, `convergence.py`, `steps/` subdirectory, or (b) explicitly note these as deliberate architectural deviations from spec with rationale and update the spec accordingly.\n    22→\n    23→This acceptance record implements option (b) of the recommended correction.\n    24→\n    25→---\n    26→\n    27→## 2. Disposition: ACCEPTED — No Roadmap Revert Required\n    28→\n    29→DEV-001 is formally accepted as an intentional architectural deviation. The roadmap's file structure is **not a defect** relative to the spec; it is the output of a valid adversarial debate process that produced a design superior to the spec's original layout. Reverting the roadmap to the spec's flat module structure would discard validated architectural improvements with no engineering benefit.\n    30→\n    31→The correct remediation is to update the spec to reflect the roadmap's accepted architecture, not to change the roadmap.\n    32→\n    33→---\n    34→\n    35→## 3. Evidence of Valid Adversarial Process\n    36→\n    37→The roadmap was produced through a two-round adversarial debate between Opus-Architect (Variant A) and Haiku-Architect (Variant B), achieving a convergence score of 0.72. The debate is fully documented in `debate-transcript.md`. The base variant (Opus-Architect, score 81 vs. 74) was selected via a scored evaluation documented in `base-selection.md`. Each sub-decision within DEV-001 traces to one or more debate decision points.\n    38→\n    39→### Sub-Decision 1: `steps/` Subdirectory Layout (D-02)\n    40→\n    41→**Debate point**: D-02 / D-04 — \"Module Layout (steps/ subdirectory vs. flat + executor.py)\"\n    42→\n    43→**Variant A position**: The `steps/` subdirectory creates a 1:1 mapping between the 7 pipeline steps and their implementation files. This is the most intuitive layout for a system whose primary abstraction is a 7-step sequential pipeline. Developers navigating the codebase will immediately understand which file implements which step.\n    44→\n    45→**Variant B position**: A flat layout with a dedicated `executor.py` follows single-responsibility more faithfully. The `steps/` subdirectory is a reasonable organizational choice, but it does not address the executor question.\n    46→\n    47→**Consensus reached (debate-transcript.md, Convergence Assessment, item 1)**:\n    48→> \"Both variants agree that an explicit `executor.py` is warranted given the complexity of orchestration (convergence, budget, resume, review gates). Variant A's `steps/` subdirectory combined with Variant B's `executor.py` is the consensus layout.\"\n    49→\n    50→**Base-selection.md confirmation** (Must-Incorporate table):\n    51→> \"Explicit `executor.py` module (D-04): Add `executor.py` to A's module list; extract orchestration logic from `cli.py`\"\n    52→\n    53→**Architectural superiority over spec**: The spec's flat layout places 7 step implementations alongside support modules with no visual or structural distinction between them. The `steps/` subdirectory provides immediate navigability (step N is in `steps/<step_name>.py`), enables step-level test isolation, and cleanly separates step logic from orchestration and support concerns. The consensus `steps/` + `executor.py` hybrid is architecturally superior to the spec's flat layout.\n    54→\n    55→### Sub-Decision 2: `convergence.py` with `ConvergenceState` Enum (D-11)\n    56→\n    57→**Debate point**: D-11 — \"Convergence as State Machine\"\n    58→\n    59→**Variant A position**: The convergence predicate (check markers, evaluate, decide) is functionally equivalent to a state machine without the formalism overhead. Three states and two transitions do not warrant formal state-machine architecture.\n    60→\n    61→**Variant B position**: The convergence loop has more states and transitions than Variant A acknowledged. READY, ITERATING, CHECKING, CONVERGED, ESCALATED, FAILED, INTERRUPTED, RESUMING — each with different invariants. A state machine makes transitions explicit, testable, and auditable.\n    62→\n    63→**Consensus reached (debate-transcript.md, D-11 Rebuttal, Variant B)**:\n    64→> \"I accept that a full state-machine framework (state classes, dispatcher, transition table) may be over-engineering. A simpler approach: use an enum for states, a dictionary for valid transitions, and assert valid transitions at each step. This is 20-30 lines of code that provides the safety guarantees without framework overhead.\"\n    65→\n    66→**Convergence Assessment confirmation** (item 5):\n    67→> \"Partial convergence. Both agree that explicit state transition documentation is necessary. Variant B's lightweight enum + valid-transition-dictionary approach is a reasonable middle ground between a predicate and a full state machine framework.\"\n    68→\n    69→**Base-selection.md confirmation** (Must-Incorporate table):\n    70→> \"Lightweight state-transition enum for convergence (D-11): Add to `convergence.py` — define `ConvergenceState` enum with `READY`, `ITERATING`, `CONVERGED`, `ESCALATED`, `FAILED`; add transition validation\"\n    71→\n    72→**Architectural superiority over spec**: The spec's approach embeds convergence logic inline in the executor via `_run_convergence_step`. This conflates orchestration responsibility with convergence state management, makes edge-case transitions implicit, and prevents isolated testing of convergence behavior. A dedicated `convergence.py` with an explicit `ConvergenceState` enum and valid-transition dictionary makes all reachable states enumerable, all transitions auditable, and all state invariants testable in isolation.\n    73→\n    74→### Sub-Decision 3: `resume.py` as Dedicated Module (D-12)\n    75→\n    76→**Debate point**: D-12 — \"Resume Design Timing (Phase 3 vs. Phase 0)\"\n    77→\n    78→**Variant A position**: Resume support can be introduced in Phase 3. The `PortifyResult` method `resume_command()` covers the spec's requirements. Adding a separate module is premature.\n    79→\n    80→**Variant B position**: Resume semantics affect the data model, the contract schema, and every step's output format. The resume decision table — which steps are re-runnable, which require prior context injection — must be defined before prompt builders are implemented. Resumability is a cross-cutting concern for a 7-step pipeline where Steps 5-7 involve expensive Claude subprocesses likely to fail.\n    81→\n    82→**Consensus reached (debate-transcript.md, D-12 Rebuttal, Variant A)**:\n    83→> \"I concede that the resume decision table (which steps are re-runnable, what context they need) should be drafted before Phase 3 — but it does not require Phase 0 to produce it. It can be a Phase 2 deliverable alongside subprocess infrastructure.\"\n    84→\n    85→**Variant B acceptance**:\n    86→> \"The resume decision table as a Phase 2 deliverable is a reasonable compromise — it does not need to be Phase 0, but it must precede prompt builder implementation for Steps 3-7.\"\n    87→\n    88→**Convergence Assessment confirmation** (item 3):\n    89→> \"Both agree the resume decision table should be a Phase 2 deliverable — before prompt builders for Steps 3-7 are implemented, but not requiring a full Phase 0 investment.\"\n    90→\n    91→**Architectural superiority over spec**: The spec treats resume as methods on `PortifyResult` (`resume_command()`, `_resume_phase()`, `_resume_substep()`). This collocates resume logic with the result representation, violating single-responsibility. The resume decision table is a cross-cutting concern: it governs which steps can be re-entered, what prior-context injection is needed, and what partial artifacts must be preserved. A dedicated `resume.py` module separates resume policy (which steps are resumable and how) from result representation (what the output looked like), and ensures that prompt builders in Steps 3-7 are designed with resumability in mind from the start.\n    92→\n    93→### Sub-Decision 4: `contract.py` — Return Contract Emission (Opus Original, Unchallenged)\n    94→\n    95→**Debate origin**: This module was introduced in the Opus-Architect roadmap (Variant A) as an original design decision. It was not challenged during the two debate rounds and thus carries unchallenged architect authority.\n    96→\n    97→**Design rationale** (from roadmap.md Phase 2):\n    98→The `to_contract()` method in the spec is defined as a method on `PortifyResult`. Variant A extracted this to a dedicated `contract.py` module to separate return contract emission — the act of producing the Phase Contracts schema YAML — from the result data model, which represents execution state. The contract is a cross-cutting output consumed by callers of the CLI; it should not be tightly coupled to the internal representation of the result object.\n    99→\n   100→**Architectural superiority over spec**: Separating `to_contract()` into `contract.py` follows the single-responsibility principle: `models.py` owns data representation; `contract.py` owns output format translation. This also enables testing contract emission independently of the result data model, and allows the contract schema to evolve without touching the result class.\n   101→\n   102→### Sub-Decision 5: `monitor.py` Merge — TUI + JSONL Logging + Signals (D-14 / Debate-Silent)\n   103→\n   104→**Debate origin**: The merge of `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, and `diagnostics.py` into `monitor.py` was not explicitly debated as a standalone point, but is architecturally coherent and consistent with the debate's overall direction toward fewer, more cohesive modules. The D-14 debate on additive-only enforcement further confirmed the pattern of consolidating monitoring and output concerns.\n   105→\n   106→**Design rationale**: The spec defines three separate modules:\n   107→- `tui.py` — Rich live dashboard with gate state machine\n   108→- `logging_.py` — Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging\n   109→- `diagnostics.py` — DiagnosticCollector, FailureClassifier, ReportGenerator\n   110→\n   111→All three are output and monitoring concerns. They share the same runtime event stream, the same lifecycle (initialized at pipeline start, closed at pipeline end), and the same consumers (the user's terminal and the execution log). Splitting them into three files creates artificial separation: a TUI event must be both rendered (tui.py) and logged (logging_.py); a diagnostic must be both generated (diagnostics.py) and surfaced to the TUI (tui.py). This creates circular dependency pressure and requires careful event routing between modules.\n   112→\n   113→A single `monitor.py` — handling Rich TUI output, JSONL logging, and domain signal processing — is a coherent, cohesive unit. The consolidation is explicitly reflected in the roadmap: \"monitor.py — Rich TUI + JSONL logging + 5 signal types.\"\n   114→\n   115→**Architectural note**: The `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, and `ReportGenerator` classes are not lost — they become internal components within `monitor.py`. Their functionality is fully preserved; only their module boundary is changed.\n   116→\n   117→### Sub-Decision 6: `cli.py` Naming (vs. `commands.py`)\n   118→\n   119→**Design rationale**: The spec uses `commands.py` following Click's convention of naming files after the Click command objects they contain. The roadmap uses `cli.py`, which names the file after its functional role (CLI entry point) rather than its Click implementation detail. This aligns with the broader Python naming convention where entry-point modules are named for their function (`cli.py`, `main.py`, `app.py`) rather than their framework abstraction. This is a minor naming alignment, not an architectural change.\n   120→\n   121→---\n   122→\n   123→## 4. Validity of the Adversarial Process\n   124→\n   125→The adversarial debate process that produced these decisions meets the standard for valid architectural consensus:\n   126→\n   127→- **Two independent architects**: Opus-Architect (Variant A) and Haiku-Architect (Variant B) produced fully independent roadmaps before the debate.\n   128→- **Two rounds**: Initial positions (Round 1) and rebuttals (Round 2) ensured each position was stress-tested against its counterpart's strongest objections.\n   129→- **Convergence scored**: A convergence score of 0.72 was computed from the debate, indicating substantial but not complete agreement — an honest outcome, not a rubber stamp.\n   130→- **Base variant selected with scoring**: Variant A was selected as the base with a weighted score of 81 vs. 74, using 8 scored criteria with documented weights and evidence.\n   131→- **Improvements incorporated**: The base-selection document explicitly lists which Variant B elements were incorporated (Must-Incorporate) and which were excluded (Do Not Incorporate) with rationale.\n   132→\n   133→The process is documented, transparent, and reproducible. These decisions were not made unilaterally; they emerged from structured disagreement between two architecturally distinct designs.\n   134→\n   135→---\n   136→\n   137→## 5. Affected Spec Sections\n   138→\n   139→The following spec sections describe the original (pre-debate) architecture and must be updated to reflect the accepted architecture:\n   140→\n   141→| Spec Section | Content Requiring Update | Priority |\n   142→|---|---|---|\n   143→| Section 4.1 — New Files table | Replace the 13-file flat layout with the 14-module roadmap layout | Required before implementation |\n   144→| Section 4.4 — Module dependency graph | Replace the spec's flat dependency graph with the `steps/` + `executor.py` graph | Required before implementation |\n   145→| Section 4.5 — Data Models | Note that `to_contract()` is extracted to `contract.py`; note `resume.py` owns the resume decision table | Recommended |\n   146→| Appendix D.2 — Executor pseudocode | Update to reflect `executor.py` as the orchestrator, with `steps/` imports | Recommended |\n   147→\n   148→---\n   149→\n   150→## 6. Spec Amendment Table\n   151→\n   152→The following table specifies the exact changes required in each section. These amendments bring the spec into alignment with the accepted roadmap architecture.\n   153→\n   154→### Amendment A: Section 4.1 — New Files Table\n   155→\n   156→**Action**: Replace the existing 13-file flat module table with the following 14-module layout.\n   157→\n   158→**Current spec Section 4.1 table** (to be replaced):\n   159→\n   160→| File | Purpose |\n   161→|---|---|\n   162→| `cli_portify/__init__.py` | Package init |\n   163→| `cli_portify/commands.py` | Click CLI group and `run` subcommand |\n   164→| `cli_portify/models.py` | Domain data models |\n   165→| `cli_portify/config.py` | Config validation step |\n   166→| `cli_portify/executor.py` | Step orchestration and execution loop |\n   167→| `cli_portify/gates.py` | Gate criteria and semantic check registry |\n   168→| `cli_portify/process.py` | Claude subprocess abstraction |\n   169→| `cli_portify/prompts.py` | Prompt builder functions for Steps 3-7 |\n   170→| `cli_portify/monitor.py` | OutputMonitor with domain signals |\n   171→| `cli_portify/tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine |\n   172→| `cli_portify/logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging |\n   173→| `cli_portify/diagnostics.py` | DiagnosticCollector, FailureClassifier, ReportGenerator |\n   174→| `cli_portify/pipeline_steps.py` | Step implementations for Steps 1-7 |\n   175→\n   176→**Replacement spec Section 4.1 table** (accepted architecture):\n   177→\n   178→| File | Purpose | Debate Basis |\n   179→|---|---|---|\n   180→| `cli_portify/__init__.py` | Package init | (unchanged) |\n   181→| `cli_portify/cli.py` | Click CLI group and `run` subcommand; registers command with `main.py` | Naming convention alignment |\n   182→| `cli_portify/executor.py` | Step orchestration loop: convergence iteration, budget management, resume state, review-gate pauses, dry-run termination | D-04 consensus |\n   183→| `cli_portify/models.py` | Domain data models: `PortifyConfig`, `ComponentInventory`, `PortifyResult`, `StepResult` (with `resumable` flag and `resume_context`) | Phase 1 foundation |\n   184→| `cli_portify/contract.py` | Return contract emission: `to_contract()` producing Phase Contracts schema YAML on all exit paths | Opus original |\n   185→| `cli_portify/resume.py` | Resume decision table: per-step resumability classification, prior-context injection rules, partial-artifact preservation policy | D-12 consensus |\n   186→| `cli_portify/convergence.py` | Convergence controller: `ConvergenceState` enum (`READY`, `ITERATING`, `CONVERGED`, `ESCALATED`, `FAILED`) with valid-transition dictionary and transition assertion | D-11 consensus |\n   187→| `cli_portify/gates.py` | Gate criteria registry: 7 `GateCriteria` objects with `SemanticCheck` compositions, tiered enforcement (EXEMPT/STANDARD/STRICT) | (unchanged) |\n   188→| `cli_portify/process.py` | Claude subprocess abstraction: `@path` references, `--add-dir`, timeout, model propagation | (unchanged) |\n   189→| `cli_portify/prompts.py` | Prompt builder functions for Steps 3-7; resume-context-aware for Steps 5-7 | Phase 2 |\n   190→| `cli_portify/monitor.py` | Unified monitoring: Rich TUI live dashboard, JSONL + Markdown execution logging, 5 signal types; contains `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` as internal components | D-14 / coherence |\n   191→| `cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py` | Step 1: config validation, name derivation, output-dir writability, collision detection | D-02 consensus |\n   192→| `cli_portify/steps/discover_components.py` | Step 2: component discovery, line counting (1MB cap with warning), `ComponentInventory` construction | D-02 consensus |\n   193→| `cli_portify/steps/analyze_workflow.py` | Step 3: Claude-assisted workflow analysis | D-02 consensus |\n   194→| `cli_portify/steps/design_pipeline.py` | Step 4: Claude-assisted pipeline design | D-02 consensus |\n   195→| `cli_portify/steps/synthesize_spec.py` | Step 5: Claude-assisted spec synthesis | D-02 consensus |\n   196→| `cli_portify/steps/brainstorm_gaps.py` | Step 6: Claude-assisted gap analysis | D-02 consensus |\n   197→| `cli_portify/steps/panel_review.py` | Step 7: Claude-assisted panel review with convergence loop; section hashing for additive-only enforcement | D-02 + D-14 consensus |\n   198→\n   199→**Note on module count**: The accepted architecture has 11 top-level modules + 7 `steps/` modules + `__init__.py` = 19 files total. The roadmap executive summary states \"14 new Python modules (13 core + `executor.py`)\" — this count excludes `__init__.py` and counts `steps/` as a directory, not individual files. The spec amendment should clarify the 18-module count (excluding `__init__.py`) for precision.\n   200→\n   201→### Amendment B: Section 4.4 — Module Dependency Graph\n   202→\n   203→**Action**: Replace the existing flat dependency graph with the `steps/` + executor-centered graph.\n   204→\n   205→**Current spec Section 4.4 graph** (to be replaced):\n   206→\n   207→```\n executor.py ──> convergence.py   (ConvergenceState enum + valid-transition dict)\n   236→  executor.py ──> resume.py        (resume decision table, per-step resumability)\n   237→  executor.py ──> prompts.py ─────────────────────────> (steps 3-7)\n   254→```\n   255→\n   256→**Key differences from original spec graph**:\n   257→1. `commands.py` is replaced by `cli.py` (same role, name aligned `contract.py` module in the implemented architecture. `PortifyResult` retains its data fields; contract emission is handled by `contract.py` calling into the result object. The `resume_command()`, `_resume_phase()`, and `_resume_substep()` methods on `PortifyResult` are similarly extracted to `resume.py`, which owns the resume decision table as a Phase 2 deliverable.\n   271→\n   272→---\n   273→\n   274→## 7. Gate Resolution Note\n   275→\n   276→### Why DEV-001 Does Not Require Roadmap Changes\n   277→\n   278→The spec-fidelity gate failed because it compared the roadmap's file list against the spec's Section 4.1 table and found them inconsistent. This is a correct detection: the files are different. However, the gate's recommended correction (option a: restore spec files) assumes the spec is authoritative and the roadmap is wrong. In this case, the relationship is inverted.\n   279→\n   280→The roadmap was produced after the spec. It went through two rounds of adversarial debate involving two independently authored variants. The debate produced validated improvements to the architecture. The spec was not updated to reflect these improvements before the spec-fidelity check ran. The gap is a documentation lag, not an architectural error.\n   281→\n   282→**The correct resolution path**:\n   283→\n   284→1. Apply the spec amendments defined in Section 6 of this document to the spec source file.\n   285→2. Re-run the spec-fidelity gate against the updated spec.\n   286→3. DEV-001 should not be flagged as HIGH severity after the amendments, because the spec will now describe the same file structure as the roadmap.\n   287→4. Any residual LOW-severity deviation (e.g., minor naming differences or count discrepancies) should be reviewed and resolved in a subsequent pass.\n   288→\n   289→**What should NOT happen**:\n   290→\n   291→- The roadmap should NOT be reverted to use `commands.py`, `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, `diagnostics.py`.\n   292→- The `steps/` subdirectory should NOT be collapsed to a flat layout.\n   293→- `contract.py`, `resume.py`, `convergence.py` should NOT be removed from the module list.\n   294→- `executor.py` should NOT be merged back into `cli.py`.\n   295→\n   296→All four of these anti-patterns would discard debate-validated architectural decisions and produce a weaker design.\n   297→\n   298→**Expected post-amendment gate outcome**:\n   299→\n   300→| DEV-001 sub-issue | Expected outcome after spec update |\n   301→|---|---|\n   302→| `steps/` subdirectory vs. flat layout | Resolved — spec will describe `steps/` layout |\n   303→| `cli.py` vs. `commands.py` | Resolved — spec will use `cli.py` |\n   304→| `contract.py` not in spec | Resolved — spec amendment adds `contract.py` |\n   305→| `resume.py` not in spec | Resolved — spec amendment adds `resume.py` |\n   306→| `convergence.py` not in spec | Resolved — spec amendment adds `convergence.py` |\n   307→| `monitor.py` merging `tui.py` + `logging_.py` + `diagnostics.py` | Resolved — spec amendment replaces 3 modules with 1 |\n   308→| `executor.py` as first-class module | Resolved — spec amendment adds `executor.py` explicitly |\n   309→\n   310→After the spec amendments are applied, a re-run of spec-fidelity against DEV-001's sub-issues should produce either no finding or a LOW-severity informational note about the module count change (13 spec → 19 roadmap files). That LOW-severity finding would itself be acceptable given the documented architectural rationale in this record.\n   311→\n   312→---\n   313→\n   314→## 8. Tasklist Implications\n   315→\n   316→DEV-001 acceptance produces the following tasklist-level guidance:\n   317→\n   318→- **Implementers MUST use the roadmap's file structure**, not the spec's Section 4.1 table, as the authoritative file list.\n   319→- **The `steps/` subdirectory is canonical**. Do not create `pipeline_steps.py` or place step logic in a flat layout.\n   320→- **`executor.py` is a first-class module**. Do not embed orchestration logic in `cli.py`.\n   321→- **`monitor.py` is the unified monitoring module**. Do not create separate `tui.py`, `logging_.py`, or `diagnostics.py`.\n   322→- **`convergence.py` must use the `ConvergenceState` enum** with `READY`, `ITERATING`, `CONVERGED`, `ESCALATED`, `FAILED` states and a valid-transition dictionary. A predicate-only implementation is insufficient.\n   323→- **`resume.py` must be delivered in Phase 2**, before prompt builders for Steps 3-7 are implemented.\n   324→- **The spec's data model section (4.5)** remains authoritative for field-level definitions of `PortifyConfig`, `PortifyResult`, `PortifyStatus`, `PortifyStepResult`, `PortifyOutcome`, `PortifyMonitorState` — except where DEV-001 or other accepted deviations explicitly override.\n   325→\n   326→---\n   327→\n   328→## 9. In practice in tests it is often an absolute path, but structurally it is just `str(Path)`.\n\n### Meaning of `spec_hash`\n`spec_hash` is computed as:\n\n```python\nhashlib.sha256(config.spec_file.read_bytes()).hexdigest()\n```\n\nSo:\n\n- algorithm: `SHA-256`\n- input: raw bytes of the spec file\n- stored format: lowercase hex digest\n- length: 64 characters\n\nThis same algorithm is reused in:\n- `/config/workspace/IronClaude/src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/spec_patch.py`\n\n### `fidelity_status` enum\nDerived from the `spec-fidelity` step result in `_derive_fidelity_status()`:\n\nPossible values:\n- `\"pass\"`\n- `\"fail\"`\n- `\"skipped\"`\n- `\"degraded\"`\n\nRules:\n- `PASS` + output file contains `validation_complete: false` => `\"degraded\"`\n- `PASS` otherwise => `\"pass\"`\n- `SKIPPED` => `\"skipped\"`\n- `FAIL` or `TIMEOUT` => `\"fail\"`\n\nIf the current run has no `spec-fidelity` result, `_save_state()` preserves any existing `fidelity_status`.\n\n### `validation`\n`_save_state()` does not construct `validation`; it preserves any existing `validation` key if already present.\n\nObserved/used shape in tests:\n```json\n\"validation\": {\n  \"status\": \"pass\" | \"fail\",\n  \"timestamp\": \"<ISO-8601 timestamp>\"\n}\n```\n\nThis is confirmed in:\n- `/config/workspace/IronClaude/tests/roadmap/test_backward_compat.py`\n- `/config/workspace/IronClaude/tests/roadmap/test_resume_pipeline_states.py`\n\n### `remediate`\nIf passed in, `_save_state()` writes the provided metadata. Skipping.\",\n                file=sys.stderr,\n                flush=True,\n            )\n            continue\n\n        try:\n            data = yaml.safe_load(frontmatter)\n        except yaml.YAMLError:\n            print(\n                f\"[roadmap] WARNING: Could not parse frontmatter in {path.name}. Skipping.\",\n                file=sys.stderr,\n                flush=True,\n            )\n            continue\n\n        if not isinstance(data, dict):\n            print(\n                f\"[roadmap] WARNING: Could not parse frontmatter in {path.name}. Skipping.\",\n                file=sys.stderr,\n                flush=True,\n            )\n            continue\n\n        # Check disposition: must be ACCEPTED (case-insensitive)\n        disposition = data.get(\"disposition\", \"\")\n        if not isinstance(disposition, str):\n            continue\n        if disposition.upper() != \"ACCEPTED\":\n            continue\n\n        # Check spec_update_required: must be YAML boolean true, NOT string \"true\"\n        spec_update_required = data.get(\"spec_update_required\", False)\n        if not isinstance(spec_update_required, bool):\n            continue\n        if not spec_update_required:\n            continue\n\n        # Build record\n        mtime = os.path.getmtime(filepath)\n        record = DeviationRecord(\n            id=str(data.get(\"id\", path.stem)),\n            disposition=disposition.upper(),\n            spec_update_required=True,\n            affects_spec_sections=data.get(\"affects_spec_sections\", []) or [],\n            acceptance_rationale=str(data.get(\"acceptance_rationale\", \"\")),\n            source_file=path.resolve(),\n            mtime=mtime,\n        )\n        records.append(record)\n\n    return records\n\n\ndef update_spec_hash(state_path: Path, new_hash: str) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Atomically update only spec_hash in state file.\n\n    Uses .tmp + os.replace() for atomic write on POSIX.\n    All other keys are preserved verbatim.\n\n    Raises OSError on write failure (caller must handle).\n    \"\"\"\n    text = state_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n    state = json.loads(text)\n    state[\"spec_hash\"] = new_hash\n    tmp = state_path.with_suffix(\".tmp\")\n    tmp.write_text(json.dumps(state, indent=2), encoding=\"utf-8\")\n    os.replace(str(tmp), str(state_path))\n\n\ndef prompt_accept_spec_change(\n    output_dir: Path, auto_accept: bool = False\n) -> int:\n    \"\"\"Interactive spec-change acceptance workflow.\n\n    Returns:\n        0 on success or idempotent no-op\n        1 on error (missing files, no evidence, etc.)\n    \"\"\"\n    state_path = output_dir / \".roadmap-state.json\"\n\n    # FR-2.24.1.1: Locate state file\n    if not state_path.exists():\n        print(\n            f\"No .roadmap-state.json found in {output_dir}. \"\n            \"Run `roadmap run` first.\",\n            file=sys.stderr,\n        )\n        return 1\n\n    try:\n        state = json.loads(state_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\"))\n    except (json.JSONDecodeError, OSError) as exc:\n        print(\n            f\"No .roadmap-state.json found in {output_dir}. \"\n            f\"Run `roadmap run` first. ({exc})\",\n            file=sys.stderr,\n        )\n        return 1\n\n    # FR-2.24.1.2: Recompute current spec hash\n    spec_file_str = state.get(\"spec_file\", \"\")\n    if not spec_file_str:\n        print(\"State file has no spec_file entry.\", file=sys.stderr)\n        return 1\n\n    spec_file = Path(spec_file_str)\n    if not spec_file.exists():\n        print(f\"Spec file not found: {spec_file}\", file=sys.stderr)\n        return 1\n\n    current_hash = hashlib.sha256(spec_file.read_bytes()).hexdigest()\n\n    # FR-2.24.1.3: Check for hash mismatch\n    saved_hash = state.get(\"spec_hash\")\n    if saved_hash and current_hash == saved_hash:\n        print(\"Spec hash is already current.
